From john_re at fastmail.us  Fri Aug  1 06:12:02 2008
From: john_re at fastmail.us (john_re)
Date: Fri, 01 Aug 2008 06:12:02 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Who's in charge of this group? - Inter group meeting
 BerkeleyTIP-Global August 2 Saturday
Message-ID: <1217596322.5803.1266497269@webmail.messagingengine.com>

Hello from Berkeley, PLUGers :)

Please tell me - who is in charge in this group?

I ask because I'm wondering: who are the person(s) who might be the ones
to help arrange & coordinate an inter group meeting?

I wonder that, because I'm putting together a great new event, a global
GNU(Linux)/BSD type software & free culture meeting.

It is a meeting for people interested in learning about, using &
creating GNU & BSD type software & culture.

I call the local Berkeley meeting the BerkeleyTIP - 
  (Talks, Installfest, Potluck & ProgrammingParty)

And I call the global simultaneous set of local meetings the
Berkeley-TIP-Global meeting.

I'm wondering
1) If anyone at your group might be interested in joining together in
this event with others around the world, and if so, then
2) who might be the person(s) to head up handling arrangements, &
coordination, etc, for the joint meeting?

If this sounds to you like it might be interesting, here is some info
for you to read:

=====  CONTENTS:
1) THE BASIC FACTS ABOUT THE MEETING
2) WHAT HAS BEEN ACCOMPLISHED SO FAR
3) WHAT TO DO NEXT
4) JOIN WITH US TOMORROW, AUGUST 2, SATURDAY
   FOR THE FIRST BerkeleyTIP-Global-USA MEETING?
5) VIDEO TALKS FOR AUGUST 2 MEETING
6) SUMMARY

=====================================================================
=====  1) THE BASIC FACTS ABOUT THE MEETING  =====

The basic idea is a monthly meeting, a full day at the beginning of each
month, the first Saturday of each month, simultaneous throughout Earth,
with these four components:

There are 4 PARALLEL TRACKS of activities:
1) TALKS        Talks by various speakers (stream/DL video globally)
2) INSTALLFEST  Bring your computer & install BSD or GNU/Linux software.
3) POTLUCK      Bring food to share or $5: eat, chat (optional)
4) PROGRAMMING PARTY     Write SW on your. or a group. project

We will have IRC & VOIP communications between the groups, enabling
information sharing, & work on development projects, etc.  It's like a
GNU-Linux user group meeting, on a global scale. Or, it's like a whole
earth GNU-Linux user group meeting.

=====================================================================
=====  2) WHAT HAS BEEN ACCOMPLISHED SO FAR  =====

I'm doing this in my "spare" part time, as a volunteer effort for the
GNU(Linux)/BSD community.  By education I'm an electrical engineer (with
a bit of computer science).  I've been a GNU(Linux) user for about 10
years, and a member of San Francisco Bay Area & Silicon Valley LUGs for
that long.

When I decided to work on doing this, about 2 months ago, I decided to
just work slowly, steadily, & build it up a step at a time.

So far, we've had two successful local meetings here in Berkeley. A
first start up meeting, just to get together & talk & plan.  Next month
we worked on getting WiFi going at the meeting so it would be easy to
share an internet connection for everyone. We also got an IRC channel up
which the meeting attendees logged into.

Now, this month, I've gotten a Google Groups mailing list & web page for
both the local, & global groups.  And, I'm now working on sending out
the announcement about this meeting, & finding out which people at other
groups are interested in this.  And I'll try to work to help groups like
yours, that have members who are interested in this, get started in
getting connected with this meeting.

=====================================================================
=====  3) WHAT TO DO NEXT  =====

So, if anyone there is interested based on what I've said so far, there
are several things that could be done:

1) Reply to this email, letting me know what part(s) of this you,
personally, are interested in.
2) As part of that, discuss among your local selves if the individuals
who are interested would like to work to get a local simultaneous
meeting going.
3) Figure out who at your group would lead that effort, or would work on
arranging it.
4) Read the Berkeley-TIP-Global website, & join it's mailing list:
http://groups.google.com/group/BerkTIPGlobal

The Global group is open to anyone joining - not just the local group
leaders.  In fact, it is _encouraged_ that everyone interested in the
meeting join the list - the input on discussions from everyone
interested will benefit everyone else.

There is more to know about this event than I can put in this email. 
I've put much of that information up on the website, so I encourage you
to scan or read it over.  Hopefully that will answer most of the
questions you have.  If not, please join that group & post questions,
comments & suggestions for improvement to the mailing list.

=====================================================================
=====  4) JOIN WITH US TOMORROW, AUGUST 2                =====
=====     FOR THE FIRST BerkeleyTIP-Global-USA MEETING?  =====

If anyone in your group is a bit experienced, or up for some fun, you
might want to pull a meeting together & join with us tomorrow, Saturday
for our first effort to have a multi-site meeting.

This month, I'm just focusing on getting the word out to USA groups.  I
call this month the Global-USA effort.  In future months I'll expand it
to working to get groups connected from the Americas, Europe, then Asia.

It's easy to join in with us - 
1) Just find someplace with at least internet capability for IRC (better
if it could do VOIP, but that's not necessary for the first meeting) -
it could be merely someone's home or apartment, an internet cafe, or a
school or office room.
2) Post an announcement to your local list that everyone is invited.
3) Come to your local meeting & get on IRC with us.
4) Download some videos & watch them simultaneously with all the
participating groups.
5) Talk about the videos, or whatever, on IRC, or VOIP.

That's all there is to it.

=====================================================================
=====  5) VIDEO TALKS FOR AUGUST 2 MEETING  =====

For this first meeting, tomorrow, Saturday, I've scheduled the following
videos to watch (All times Pacific Daylight Savings Time, adjust for
local time accordingly.):

TENTATIVE SCHEDULE: 

1000 AM--------------------------------------------------------------
Network1:  Asterisk VOIP - Sameer Verma
                http://video.google.com/videoplay?docid=-2148055040572903738
                http://www.penlug.org/twiki/bin/view/Home/MeetingAgenda20070628

                http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=EJKe_jXszFc

                http://youtube.com/watch?v=bDgD9whDfEY
                http://mail.python.org/pipermail/baypiggies/2008-June/003629.html

                http://video.google.com/videoplay?docid=-2199332044603874737

                http://video.google.com/videoplay?docid=-2765503550413131030

                http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IPabiIHgmBU

=====================================================================
=====  6) SUMMARY  =====

Well, that is the basic information.

Does this sound interesting to you?  Please reply to this email & let me
know.

I look forward to hearing from you. :)

http://groups.google.com/group/BerkTIPGlobal


From qhartman at gmail.com  Fri Aug  1 11:04:20 2008
From: qhartman at gmail.com (Quentin Hartman)
Date: Fri, 1 Aug 2008 11:04:20 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Apache2 Directory indexing in Etch not possible?
Message-ID: <8975a95f0808011104u4f2fc415p423c8ee8f8993f20@mail.gmail.com>

I need to enable directory indexing in apache2 running on Debian Etch (4.0).

After much digging, I've discovered that the mod_autoindex module
required to enable this functionality is missing. Normally, this is
compiled into the binary directly, but an "apache2 -l" reveals that it
is not. It also is not listed in the mods-available  directory, nor is
there an obvious package for it in apt.

Any thoughts? This is really basic functionality which I've never seen
so completely removed before. I assume it's a Debian thing, but The
Google reveals nothing so far...

-_-?

-- 
-Regards-

-Quentin Hartman-

From heinlein at madboa.com  Fri Aug  1 11:31:58 2008
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Fri, 1 Aug 2008 11:31:58 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Apache2 Directory indexing in Etch not possible?
In-Reply-To: <8975a95f0808011104u4f2fc415p423c8ee8f8993f20@mail.gmail.com>
References: <8975a95f0808011104u4f2fc415p423c8ee8f8993f20@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <alpine.OSX.1.10.0808011129120.98199@guild.galois.com>

On Fri, 1 Aug 2008, Quentin Hartman wrote:

> I need to enable directory indexing in apache2 running on Debian 
> Etch (4.0).
>
> After much digging, I've discovered that the mod_autoindex module 
> required to enable this functionality is missing. Normally, this is 
> compiled into the binary directly, but an "apache2 -l" reveals that 
> it is not. It also is not listed in the mods-available directory, 
> nor is there an obvious package for it in apt.

mod_autoindex isn't compiled into the etch apache2 binary; it's 
included as a loadable module in the apache2.2-common package:

   [heinlein at monk ~]$ dpkg -L apache2.2-common | grep mod_autoindex
   /usr/lib/apache2/modules/mod_autoindex.so

See also /etc/apache2/mods-available/autoindex.load.

-- 
Paul Heinlein <> heinlein at madboa.com <> http://www.madboa.com/

>   [heinlein at monk ~]$ dpkg -L apache2.2-common | grep mod_autoindex
>   /usr/lib/apache2/modules/mod_autoindex.so

I finally got to this as well. Someone had removed the .load for it
from this machine. Copied it from another install, and we are in
business. Thanks for the attention!

I wonder what folks here think about the ReactOS about page.
  http://www.reactos.org/en/about.html

It sounds to me like the ReactOS people are saying that their system
will be better than everything else, which is a little silly IMHO.
UNIX to NT is comparing apples to oranges and I think the idea that
the NT architecture is inherently more secure than Unix is debatable.

Firefox 2 won't install to ReactOS 0.3.5 and 1.5 doesn't render
properly.  I don't know where the video bugs are coming from, but
they are pretty extensive.  0.3.5 may be an improvement over 0.3.4,
but it is awfully hard to tell.

I tried to put a complaint up, didn't go so well:
http://www.reactos.org/forum/viewtopic.php?
f=18&t=5915&sid=3e10904256835959cfdd1b3f9839f6bd

     Michael Robinson

On Sat, Aug 2, 2008 at 12:16 AM, Miles Rose <milesros at peoplepc.com> wrote:
> Some web sites I use present me with a page size that isn't right-
> justified, so I have to move and resize the window. I use Mozilla
> on RedHat 8, if that helps.  Mozilla help pages don't help, and
> none of my references address the problem.  Any ideas?
>

Some people just write web pages poorly.  Or rather, whatever GUI tool
they use does it poorly.

If the problem is in their stylesheet (like maybe a hardcoded 'width'
setting) you might be able to unset the setting by turning CSS off
whenever you hit one of those pages.

If it's a page that you go to a lot, and you don't mind switching to
another browser, and learning a bit of CSS, then you can use the
'stylish' extension on Firefox to permanently restyle a page or
domain.

Ali

On 8/2/08, Ali Corbin <ali.corbin at gmail.com> wrote:

>  If it's a page that you go to a lot, and you don't mind switching to
>  another browser, and learning a bit of CSS, then you can use the
>  'stylish' extension on Firefox to permanently restyle a page or
>  domain.

heck, if you don't mind using another browser, opera has a
"fit-to-width" option that you can turn on by hitting control-f11.
nearly all pages (super-ajaxy ones discluded) will get usably
reformatted (usually by shrinking the largest images and wrapping
text) to fit to the width of your browser window.

another "easy" shortcut is to go full-screen which will hopefully make
your browser window big enough, works in ie/ff/opera.  just one
keystroke there and back---f10 (i think?  i use a window manager in
which all windows are full screen these days so i haven't had to know
that for awhile =))

need to die?  It has been around for 12 years.  It isn't a fly by
night project.  WINE is getting better, but there are still people
using Windows because program X doesn't run even under WINE in
Linux.

There's an old saying, "Don't shoot the messenger."  Now, I want
to hear why the ReactOS project should die and what people think
about the Linux is so 1970's comment among other comments on the
about page.

Here are some of the comments on the ReactOS about page:

"Despite statements to the contrary, NT is secure by design. It was  
the first mainstream operating system with a proper implementation of  
a very flexible security model based on access control lists."

"UNIX operating system adhere to the file metaphor, and devices such  
as printers, storage devices, keyboards, and monitors all appear as  
ordinary files to both programmers and regular users. This simplifies  
many routine tasks, and is a key component in the extensibility of the  
system. The file metaphor has several downsides and it is known as a  
bottleneck of UNIX like operating systems.
ReactOS capitalizes on this metaphor and expands it. It uses an object  
metaphor that is pervasive throughout the architecture of the system.  
Not only are all of the things in the UNIX file metaphor viewed as  
objects by ReactOS, but so are things such as processes and threads,  
shared memory segments, the global registry database and even access  
rights."

"MacOS X, Linux, BSD flavors and other UNIX derivates share a common  
heritage based on a more than three decades old design of a simple  
basic operating system, that has evolved over time into a complex  
structure.
Modern incarnations like Mac OS X put a fancy graphical user interface  
on top of UNIX, to hide system details and focus mainly for beginners  
and likely advanced users are left out in the rain. In contrast,  
various Linux and BSD flavors have been put together originally for  
server usage and are therefore very console centric. Most advanced  
features cannot be accessed from the basic graphical user interface.  
Almost all UNIX flavors retain some of the original design flaws and  
binary compatibility between various versions is usually non-existent.

In theory there are a few UNIX standards like POSIX but in practice  
the standards are old and cover only the basic operating system and  
the terminal environment. Other standards such as the Linux Standard  
Base are often not implemented faithfully. As there is no user  
interface standard nor a standard API, most people still have to use  
command line applications or fight through the GUI mess. Many UNIX  
derivates use the de-facto standard X-Window system for graphical  
output, which might well possess one of the worst designs in software  
history.
Still, modern UNIX derivates are trying to catch up with recent  
innovations and some of them already possess important features like  
access control list support."

      Michael C. Robinson

Linux Plumbers Conference

Linux Plumbers Conference is a local Portland conference that will take
place September 17th-19th.  We are targeting developers working on the
low level programming of Linux, including the kernel, libraries, and
system applications such as udev, hal, and dbus.  We came up with the
name "Plumbers" because we wanted to represent these areas as the basic
system infrastructure.  We also wanted this to be a working conference,
where people solve plumbing problems instead of just yammering at each
other.

Linux Plumbers Conference
17-19 September 2008
Smith Memorial Student Union
Portland, Oregon USA
http://www.linuxplumbersconf.org/

Early bird registration ends on August 18th, so register at
http://linuxplumbersreg.eventbrite.com/ before the registration fee
increases from $250 to $300!



Linux Plumbers Conference Student Day

LPC is also hosting a Student Day, catering to students who want to work
on plumbing infrastructure.  The Student Day includes hands-on tutorials
from local open source developers, an introduction to the open source
communities represented at the Linux Plumbers Conference, and a career
panel comprised of local open source companies.

Linux Plumbers Conference Student Day
16 September 2008, 9:00-17:00
Portland State Business Accelerator
Portland, Oregon USA
http://www.linuxplumbersconf.org/program/students/

The $50 student registration fee includes admission to the Linux
Plumbers Conference, the Tuesday evening IBM-sponsored event at Aura
Lounge with Linux Kernel Summit attendees, and the Wednesday night
Intel-sponsored event at the Portland Art Museum.  Students should
register at http://linuxplumbersreg.eventbrite.com/

Students who wish to attend LPC Student Day must have been registered
as a full-time student for the last term of the 2007-2008 school year,
or be registered as a full-time student for the Summer 2008 or Fall 2008
term.

I have a few questions
Why is Cox relaying a message supposedly from a Hotmail user? It should be
coming from a Hotmail server.
What type of sender verification do you have configured in Postfix?

It's likely contacting Hotmail, doing a basic EHLO, and RCPT TO: for that
user.. if Hotmail says no, then the sender verify has failed, and Postfix is
rejecting it.
Is someuser a valid account on Hotmail?

> On Sun, Aug 3, 2008 at 2:08 PM, robinson-west user

> > math requirements alone, CS is extremely challenging.  I guess I'm
> > wondering why part time students are excluded?
> 
> We mostly wanted to make sure someone wasn't trying to get a lowered
> admissions price because they were just taking a PE class.  I'll talk it
> over with the conference organizers and see if they're up for allowing
> part time students to attend Student Day.  Would requiring students to
> be registered for four credits or more seem like a reasonable
> requirement?

First, whatever registration requirement you decide on, how do you plan
to verify it? For example, I have a PSU student ID card, a pdx.edu
e-mail account, and an ODIN account, yet I am not registered for any
courses at all this (summer) term.

Second, Portland State is an urban university. Its enrollment is 32%
graduate students, who mostly take only one or two courses at a time
because they have full time jobs. And that goes for about half the
undergraduates as well. The average undergraduate at PSU takes six
years to complete the degree.

Third, if you are taking a PE course at PSU it is probably because your
are a PE major, so it is a regular full course with the usual academic
rigor. 

I understand your intent; I merely wish to point out that enforcing it
by requiring that a person be currently registered for a particular
number of hours may be impractical. I would suggest that you use the
same standard as commercial software companies do when offering
academic prices for their software - which is just an ID card with a
student number.

From robert.citek at gmail.com  Mon Aug  4 21:11:40 2008
From: robert.citek at gmail.com (Robert Citek)
Date: Mon, 4 Aug 2008 23:11:40 -0500
Subject: [PLUG] question
In-Reply-To: <1217907580.23690.10.camel@localhost>
References: <323326.47378.qm@web56603.mail.re3.yahoo.com>
	<1217907580.23690.10.camel@localhost>
Message-ID: <4145b6790808042111i3c9a3979k4f3855503c3cd354@mail.gmail.com>

In ascii art form:

Debian --{switch}-- Ubuntu--{modem}---{ISP}

How is your modem connecting to the ISP?  PPPoE?  Straight DHCP?
Static IP?  Something else?

What version of Ubuntu are you using?

Whomever it is your ISP has to assign you an IP address, gateway,
netmask, DNS, etc.  They'll either write it down for you or assign it
to you dynamically.

Regards,
- Robert

From seniorr at aracnet.com  Mon Aug  4 21:57:00 2008
From: seniorr at aracnet.com (Russell Senior)
Date: 04 Aug 2008 21:57:00 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] question
In-Reply-To: <1217910117.23690.26.camel@localhost>
References: <323326.47378.qm@web56603.mail.re3.yahoo.com>
	<1217907580.23690.10.camel@localhost>
	<4145b6790808042111i3c9a3979k4f3855503c3cd354@mail.gmail.com>
	<1217910117.23690.26.camel@localhost>
Message-ID: <861w14ys83.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>

>>>>> "linux-yug" == linux-yug  <linux-yug at xprt.net> writes:

linux-yug> On Mon, 2008-08-04 at 23:11 -0500, Robert Citek wrote:
>> In ascii art form:
>> 
>> Debian --{switch}-- Ubuntu--{modem}---{ISP}
>> 


linux-yug> nice drawing... I assign static IPs to both ethernet cards
linux-yug> connecting to switch..

>> How is your modem connecting to the ISP?  PPPoE?  Straight DHCP?
>> Static IP?  Something else?
>> 

linux-yug> I connect to ISP via PPP..  AND I get a dynamic IP

You want the Ubuntu box to NAT for you.  The ISP is assigning you one
IP address and that's all it know about.  So, you need an iptables
rule something like:

  iptables -t nat -I PREROUTING -o ppp0 -j MASQUERADE

if you don't already.


-- 
Russell Senior         ``I have nine fingers; you have ten.''
seniorr at aracnet.com

Don't forget to turn on ip forwarding

From johnxj at comcast.net  Tue Aug  5 21:11:04 2008
From: johnxj at comcast.net (John Jason Jordan)
Date: Tue, 5 Aug 2008 21:11:04 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] thinkpads off the shelf in portland?
In-Reply-To: <86ljzb2gbs.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
References: <86ljzb2gbs.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
Message-ID: <20080805211104.d38ce880.johnxj@comcast.net>

On 05 Aug 2008 16:27:19 -0700
Russell Senior <russell at personaltelco.net> dijo:

> An old laptop my boss uses died today on the eve of a trip on which he
> needs one.  Where in town can we lay our hands on a thinkpad in a
> hurry?

I got mine at Computek, 1615 SW Jefferson, Portland, 503-274-4384. They
are an authorized Lenovo dealer. Most of the Thinkpads they sell are
custom orders for local businesses, but they do keep a few in stock.
Unlike big box stores, they know Thinkpads, as that is about all they
sell. They are a small outfit, but have been in business in Portland
for at least a decade. They specialize in selling to businesses that
need special high end computers that are also reliable. When I was
buying my T61 the salesperson knew all the options it had, what
hardware was inside, what I could get instead if I custom ordered a
Thinkpad, and even how long different options would take to arrive.
When I said that its stock 1 GB RAM was not enough he said he could add
whatever I wanted up to its max of 4 GB. I opted for 2 GB and he just
did it while I waited.

Their salesmanship is somewhat aloof, but it's a pleasure to buy from a
salesperson who knows the product. And before buying the T61 from them
I priced it on Lenovo's site, and the Lenovo online price was only a
few dollars cheaper than Computek's price.

I bought it on a Saturday and just left it in the box because the next
day was a Clinic. I opened the box at the Clinic and we baptized it
into the world of Linux and OSS.

# from Roderick A. Anderson
# on Wednesday 06 August 2008 16:54:

>So I'm now looking for suggestions/experience with USB connected
>headsets -- microphone and headphone combination. ?I get the feeling
>most will just work as there is very little current info when I search
>using Google.

Yep.  The USB sound standard seems to have gotten something right.

I have a logitech a-0374a, which is fine for sound quality (the 
microphone is particularly fine), but I'm always afraid I'll yank the 
thinner wire out of the set given the way the heavier usb cable 
terminates at a clip 24" from my ear -- I guess that goes on your belt 
if you wear your pants real high, but I never know what to do with the 
silly thing.  And apparently the volume buttons don't work.   The mute 
button is ok.  Said buttons are found on the aforementioned silly clip 
and therefore contribute to the weight of the usb cable which is 
pulling on the skinny $30 part of the cable :-/

I wanted a bluetooth headset merely because I hate cables. I was always
coming close to hanging myself with them. Suddenly ripping the headset
off my head as I inadvertently snagged one of the cables was also not
amusing.

I wanted a headset that was of professional audiophile quality. I
wasn't concerned with the phone at all. I'm not very popular, so no one
calls me anyway. I bought the Sony BT50 headset on Amazon and they work
fine with the bluetooth in my Thinkpad T61. I also got an after-market
device that plugs into my iPod so it can transmit via bluetooth. It
works great with the BT50 headset too. Now I can sit and listen to
symphonies from my computer, or listen to them from my iPod while
hiking.

I also bought a bluetooth device that supposedly allows you to transmit
via bluetooth from your computer to a home audio system. It has
standard RCA plugs that go into an AUX input on the amplifier. It
works, but the sound is strangely distorted. 

Having said all of that, I discovered one small problem using the
computer and the headset. The headset works fine with all programs
except Realplayer. My dim understanding is that it is because
Realplayer does not use ALSA. I tried a number of things - including a
utility that is supposed to convert, but nothing has worked.
Unfortunately, some streaming radio stations do not work in open source
alternatives to Realplayer. I mention this only because you mentioned
having problems getting ALSA to recognize the earpiece. It could be
that my problem with OSS is related.

a potential workaround for naughty audio apps is to use them via
esddsp or artsdsp if you can run the enlightened sound daemon (from
the gnome folks) or kde's sound daemon arts.  i used that to make some
software behave better (specifically, the !@#$ flash plugin that liked
to hang my whole browser if the audio devices were in use).

the wrapper programs (artsdsp or esddsp) did some magic to reroute
sound device interaction via arts or esound--not sure how well it
would work if the program actually doesn't go via the sound drivers at
all--but if it just uses OSS instead of ALSA, there's probably a
decent chance, worth trying anyway.

Subject: [PLUG] Reading HPFS/NTFS drive

My brother-in-law sent me a used computer. There's something wrong with
the box because it won't boot, or even get as far as the BIOS. I'm
trying to discover what parts I can use.

As far as I know, he's never used Linux, so I expect the drive to have
some M$ file system on it. I installed it in my USB enclosure and
connected it to my Linux machine. I get a Konqueror window that tells me
that it was mounted on media:/sda1/. It has one directory named "System
Volume Information" and inside that are two objects, one named
"MountPointManagerRemoteDatabase" which Konqueror says is an empty
document, and a binary file named "tracking.log" which Konqueror says is
20.0 KB. I know it to be a binary from trying to look at it with
Konqueror and being told that it is a binary file, and that I would
corrupt it if I saved it.

Should I be able to see more than that?

The partitioner in YaST says:

Device     Size     F  Type            Start  End      Device ID
/dev/sda   28.6 GB     Maxtor 6-E030LO        3637    usb-Maxtor_6_E030LO_0
/dev/sda1  28.6 GB     HPFS/NTFS           0  3736   
usb-Maxtor_6_E030LO_0-part1

In the long run, it doesn't matter to me if I can read anything on that
drive or not. I'm just curious to know more about the drive before I
install Ubuntu on it.

Might I suggest booting with knoppix, just because it is all set up to
be able to mount NTFS patitions (kernel support, etc).  I have used
knoppix to rescue data from winblows boxes more than once, and it is
always a breeze to mount and read.

Or make sure you have NTFS support in your running kernel.  The module
is called ntfs, according to my kernel docs.

If there really is a winblows load on sda1, you should see a lot more
than System Volume Information.  Maybe you are seeing accurate
information if someone tried to delete everything from within winblows.

Or just reformat the drive with a suitable linux filesystem (like ext3)
and run badblocks on it, if all you care about is verifying the
usability of the drive.

Carlos Konstanski

From ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com  Fri Aug  8 12:38:32 2008
From: ckonstanski at pippiandcarlos.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Fri, 8 Aug 2008 13:38:32 -0600
Subject: [PLUG] Meaning of binary was:  Reading HPFS/NTFS drive
In-Reply-To: <489C8414.90703@pacifier.com>
References: <489C79C1.9080207@comcast.net>
	<489C8414.90703@pacifier.com>
Message-ID: <18588.41144.801938.264672@sphinktop.pippiandcarlos.com>

Wayne E. Van Loon Sr. writes:
 > Richard and all:
 > I don't have anything to offer in the way of help, sorry. But I am 
 > curious about something and wonder if someone can help me understand.
 > As I understand it, files that are compiled / assembled are usually 
 > referred to as "binary" (for some reason that makes no sense to me). 
 > Maybe a misnomer that has stuck?
 > 
 > I wonder if Konqueror is unable to interpret files in the file systems 
 > and therefore tags it as a "binary" file. I also wouldn't expect a log 
 > file to be a "binary" - unless binary has other meanings in other contexts.
 > Wayne

Binary files are just plain files.  There is no concept of lines.
Such a concept only has meaning when dealing with text that a human
can read (stories, source code, log files).  Even if a file contains
only ASCII characters, it is not necessarily a text file.  A
BASE64-encoded MIME attachments is ASCII, but it is not
human-readable, and has no end of line markers.  Also consider an
ASCII-encoded GPG key.

Some binary files (files without line demarcations) are used to store
natively executable code, or executable bytecode.  These are
executable binaries.  There are also executable text files, which are
ASCII files, containing human-readable text (and lines!), the contents
of which happen to be parseable and interpretable by some language
engine, like perl or bash.

I will hang it out there and make a guess that binary files are called
that for this reason: the contents are interesting at a bit-wide
level.  It is fun to observe the bit patterns in machine code words,
and doing so will shed much light on why the various codes have the
values they do.  Compression works at the bit level, and the resulting
files need to convey that.  Bitmaps are an obvious, self-explanatory
example.

Many programs (konqueror may or may not be one of these, but I suspect
it is) use MIME mappings to decide what type of data a file contains.
This just means that it uses the filename extension as its one and
only clue.  You can go into such programs and change the MIME mappings
if you want; it's just a dumb hash table.  On the other hand, the
"file" command line program actually looks at the file header.
-- 
Carlos

From tkubaska at easystreet.net  Sat Aug  9 11:12:25 2008
From: tkubaska at easystreet.net (Ted Kubaska (easy))
Date: Sat, 09 Aug 2008 11:12:25 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] why does this 553 error occur when I send mail
Message-ID: <1218305545.13342.11.camel@localhost>


I got to mention Joomla/VirtueMart but my mail is really about email
operation.

Joomla is a CMS and VirtueMart is an e-commerce package for it. There's
a bunch of email that goes back and forth when a customer buys stuff.

When a customer buys a product, VirtueMart sends the customer a
confirmation email. It sends this email to the email address that the
customer registered with. This works fine. 

Virtuemart then also sends an email to the store. You configure the
store's email, which in my case is a gmail account. When I look at the
mail received by that account, I see that it is from the email address
that the customer registered with. This sometimes works and sometimes
does not. 

When it does not work, the error message is 
"553 sorry, your mail was administratively denied. (#5.7.1)"
This error message is sent to the customer's email address.

It is dependent on what the customer's email address is. I have two test
customers. They are both me with different names. They are identical
except for their email addresses. For one customer (whose email address
is from a DSL provider), everything works. For the other customer (whose
email address is from a cable provider), it fails with that 553 error. I
have both DSL and cable providers.

If I use an email client (Evolution) I can mail from the customer's
cable address (which is my own cable email address) to the store's email
address (which is a gmail address).

I've talked to both my hoster (godaddy) and my ISP (comcast) and neither
is able to help. And I've posted on the VirtueMart forum with more
questions about the internals of VirtueMart in that post. But I don't
think it's a VirtueMart problem ... I think it's something that comcast
is doing.

And so I'm looking at ways to modify the PHP code that does the sending
(PHPmailer is included with VirtueMart) to workaround the problem, but
this is difficult because I don't know why I see this problem and hence
where I should look.
 -ted

One cheeseball method I have used in the past with PHP is to add the -f
switch to the mail() function call.  This sets the sender address to be the
same as the recipient address.  This makes the mail server think that the
recipient is sending a mail to themself.  See if you find that PHPMailer
is, at the bottom of it all, using the standard mail() function, and try
the -f switch just for fun.  This will determine if the gmail mail
server is rejecting you solely based on the sender address.

http://devzone.zend.com/manual/function.mail.html

Set the -f switch in the additional_parameters argument of the mail()
function (the fifth argument).  This will pass the -f to sendmail.

Is the email being sent in plaintext?  You could packet-trace the two
emails and look for any differences.  By "the two emails", I mean the
Evolution-sent one vs. the webapp-sent one.  Or there's always the old
telnet email connection.  You can use a perl one-liner to generate the
AUTH string.  We can dig that up if it gets to that point.

One option would be to get the gmail mail server out of the picture: set
up your own mail server.  But then you'll start seeing the problems I
see, where I cannot send mail to customers who have yahoo accounts
because yahoo rejects emails sent from my non-isp domain name.  You
can't win in this new regime of spammers on one side, anti-spam paranoids
on the other.  But you'd think that godaddy.com would be an accepted
domain.

Carlos


From tkubaska at easystreet.net  Sat Aug  9 14:05:57 2008
From: tkubaska at easystreet.net (Ted Kubaska (easy))
Date: Sat, 09 Aug 2008 14:05:57 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] why does this 553 error occur when I send mail
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0808091217330.7047@sphinktop.pippiandcarlos.com>
References: <1218305545.13342.11.camel@localhost>
	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0808091217330.7047@sphinktop.pippiandcarlos.com>
Message-ID: <1218315957.13342.52.camel@localhost>

Thanks much Carlos. Good suggestions. In the meantime I came across a
VirtueMart enhancement request on the VM dev list that has been
implemented and that if I unimplement looks as if it might fix the
problem.

https://dev.virtuemart.net/cb/issue/2165 

It seems someone wanted the from address in the store notification to be
the customer so that whoever read the store's mail could easily reply. 

This does not sound like a good enhancement to me (and the comments on
the enhancement agree with me) but nonetheless it was implemented.

  -ted



On Sat, 2008-08-09 at 12:40 -0600, Carlos Konstanski wrote:
> On Sat, 9 Aug 2008, Ted Kubaska (easy) wrote:
> 
> > Date: Sat, 09 Aug 2008 11:12:25 -0700

> >     <plug at lists.pdxlinux.org>
> > To: "General Linux/UNIX discussion and help;	civil and on-topic"
> >     <plug at lists.pdxlinux.org>
> > Subject: [PLUG] why does this 553 error occur when I send mail
> > 
> >
> > I got to mention Joomla/VirtueMart but my mail is really about email
> > operation.
> >
> > Joomla is a CMS and VirtueMart is an e-commerce package for it. There's
> > a bunch of email that goes back and forth when a customer buys stuff.
> >
> > When a customer buys a product, VirtueMart sends the customer a
> > confirmation email. It sends this email to the email address that the
> > customer registered with. This works fine.
> >
> > Virtuemart then also sends an email to the store. You configure the
> > store's email, which in my case is a gmail account. When I look at the
> > mail received by that account, I see that it is from the email address
> > that the customer registered with. This sometimes works and sometimes
> > does not.
> >
> > When it does not work, the error message is
> > "553 sorry, your mail was administratively denied. (#5.7.1)"
> > This error message is sent to the customer's email address.
> >
> > It is dependent on what the customer's email address is. I have two test
> > customers. They are both me with different names. They are identical
> > except for their email addresses. For one customer (whose email address
> > is from a DSL provider), everything works. For the other customer (whose
> > email address is from a cable provider), it fails with that 553 error. I
> > have both DSL and cable providers.
> >
> > If I use an email client (Evolution) I can mail from the customer's
> > cable address (which is my own cable email address) to the store's email
> > address (which is a gmail address).
> >
> > I've talked to both my hoster (godaddy) and my ISP (comcast) and neither
> > is able to help. And I've posted on the VirtueMart forum with more
> > questions about the internals of VirtueMart in that post. But I don't
> > think it's a VirtueMart problem ... I think it's something that comcast
> > is doing.
> >
> > And so I'm looking at ways to modify the PHP code that does the sending
> > (PHPmailer is included with VirtueMart) to workaround the problem, but
> > this is difficult because I don't know why I see this problem and hence
> > where I should look.
> > -ted
> 
> One cheeseball method I have used in the past with PHP is to add the -f
> switch to the mail() function call.  This sets the sender address to be the
> same as the recipient address.  This makes the mail server think that the
> recipient is sending a mail to themself.  See if you find that PHPMailer
> is, at the bottom of it all, using the standard mail() function, and try
> the -f switch just for fun.  This will determine if the gmail mail
> server is rejecting you solely based on the sender address.
> 
> http://devzone.zend.com/manual/function.mail.html
> 
> Set the -f switch in the additional_parameters argument of the mail()
> function (the fifth argument).  This will pass the -f to sendmail.
> 
> Is the email being sent in plaintext?  You could packet-trace the two
> emails and look for any differences.  By "the two emails", I mean the
> Evolution-sent one vs. the webapp-sent one.  Or there's always the old
> telnet email connection.  You can use a perl one-liner to generate the
> AUTH string.  We can dig that up if it gets to that point.
> 
> One option would be to get the gmail mail server out of the picture: set
> up your own mail server.  But then you'll start seeing the problems I
> see, where I cannot send mail to customers who have yahoo accounts
> because yahoo rejects emails sent from my non-isp domain name.  You
> can't win in this new regime of spammers on one side, anti-spam paranoids
> on the other.  But you'd think that godaddy.com would be an accepted
> domain.
> 
> Carlos



From plug at the-wes.com  Sat Aug  9 15:39:56 2008
From: plug at the-wes.com (wes)
Date: Sat, 9 Aug 2008 15:39:56 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] why does this 553 error occur when I send mail
In-Reply-To: <1218315957.13342.52.camel@localhost>
References: <1218305545.13342.11.camel@localhost>
	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0808091217330.7047@sphinktop.pippiandcarlos.com>
	<1218315957.13342.52.camel@localhost>
Message-ID: <b399d1c10808091539l13204fb4s6a88df0c88d91340@mail.gmail.com>

It could be that something like SPF or DomainKeys is getting in the way.
When the store sends emails "as" the customer, this is essentially the same
as when a spammer spoofs someone else's email address. That scenario is
exactly what those two countermeasures were invented to combat. That would
explain why the results vary by domain; if the owner/operator of a given
domain does not implement spoofing countermeasures, the spoofed emails get
through unchallenged.

This also explains why the email works fine coming from Evolution; it's
(presumably) being sent out via comcast's mail server, while the email from
the ecommerce webapp is being sent out via the mail server at the same
location as the webapp is running.

-wes

From rsteff at comcast.net  Sat Aug  9 17:04:45 2008
From: rsteff at comcast.net (Richard C. Steffens)
Date: Sat, 09 Aug 2008 17:04:45 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Reading HPFS/NTFS drive
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.64.0808081118130.14370@sphinktoo.pippiandcarlos.com>
References: <489C79C1.9080207@comcast.net>
	<Pine.LNX.4.64.0808081118130.14370@sphinktoo.pippiandcarlos.com>
Message-ID: <489E309D.7000403@comcast.net>

Carlos Konstanski wrote:
> Might I suggest booting with knoppix, just because it is all set up to
> be able to mount NTFS patitions (kernel support, etc).  I have used
> knoppix to rescue data from winblows boxes more than once, and it is
> always a breeze to mount and read.
>
> Or make sure you have NTFS support in your running kernel.  The module
> is called ntfs, according to my kernel docs.
>   
# modprobe -l ntfs
/lib/modules/2.6.16.53-0.16-default/kernel/fs/ntfs/ntfs.ko

> If there really is a winblows load on sda1, you should see a lot more
> than System Volume Information.  Maybe you are seeing accurate
> information if someone tried to delete everything from within winblows.
>   
Entirely possible.
> Or just reformat the drive with a suitable linux filesystem (like ext3)
> and run badblocks on it, if all you care about is verifying the
> usability of the drive.
>   
I'll probably do that this week.

Thanks for the ideas.

-- 
Regards,

Dick Steffens
 



From denish at dslnorthwest.net  Sun Aug 10 21:02:24 2008

Subject: [PLUG] Optimizer?
Message-ID: <489FB9D0.70001@dslnorthwest.net>

While browsing, a message appeared, unannounced, uninvited, and persistent.  I
mentioned this once before on this board, but was not quick enough to capture
the details.  Now I have details.

The first window to appear:

The page at http://performanceoptimizer.com says:
NOTICE: Errors in you PC can cause data loss, hardware or software failure and
performance fall.
Install PerformanceOptimizer to fix errors, monitor changes and maintain PC
stability!

And so it goes through 3 windows.

To the best of my knowledge I did not click on anything in the page I was 
viewing.  Are these windows the result of Java script or Java?  Closing Firefox 
seems to be the best way to get rid of them, but that is a pita.

I did have a number of cookies from PerformanceOptimizer--I just deleted them. 
And I prohibited cookies from http://performanceoptimizer.com.  Will it put an 
end to this?

Is the site I am visiting when these windows show up responsible?

I have done some searching for this, but almost all hits deal with Windows, and 
are mostly old.

Any information would be appreciated.

Thanks,
-Denis

Subject: [PLUG] Need new e-mail account

For years I have used a free e-mail account at Hotpop.com for most of
my e-list activity (but not for PLUG). For the past several days I have
been unable to access my mail with Sylpheed, which normally accesses
the Hotpop account without problem. I can log in via the web and I see
183 messages. Unfortunately, Hotpop's web interface does not allow
reading mail in a browser - you have to download it with a mail client. 

This is not the first time Hotpop has done this to me. Now, since all
the messages in the inbox are either from an e-list (which are archived
online anyway), or are spam, I just deleted them all. Then I canceled
the Hotpop account. 

So now I am shopping for a replacement free e-mail account. I started
with Gmail, but I can't get it configured so that Sylpheed can download
messages. There are a lot of specific requirements and I must have one
of them off. I got it to the point where Sylpheed goes to the Gmail
account, but the GUI window then hangs. Sylpheed has a log utility so
you can see what kind of messages you are getting. When I try to
download messages I get 

* Connecting to POP3 server: pop.gmail.com...
* Incorporation cancelled

Does anyone know what incorporation is?

An additional fact: When I am at PSU I cannot send e-mail unless I send
it through mailhost at pdx.edu using my pdx.edu account. This works OK,
and it works even from home. Hence, I have always configured my e-mail
accounts in Sylpheed to download from the account's pop server, but to
send via mailhost at pdx.edu. Comcast doesn't seem to mind, and Hotpop
didn't either. On the hunch that this might be what is screwing up my
Gmail account I changed it to use smtp.gmail.com and to use my Gmail
username and password. However, that doesn't work either. I can't send
from the Gmail account any better than I can receive.

Any suggestions welcome, including suggestions for a different free
account. 


From plug_1 at robinson-west.com  Wed Aug 13 23:54:04 2008
From: plug_1 at robinson-west.com (robinson-west user)
Date: Wed, 13 Aug 2008 23:54:04 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Need new e-mail account
In-Reply-To: <20080813223941.112fa1eb.johnxj@comcast.net>
References: <20080813223941.112fa1eb.johnxj@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <1218696844.24259.8.camel@goose.robinson-west.com>

How about running your own mail server?

If you connect to the Internet via DSL, fiber optics, or
ISDN, you can do this no problem as long as you have an IP
block.  The IP block can be one IP address ;-)  I 
recommend Postfix for this and I strongly recommend setting
up a mail gateway between you and the Net that only accepts
email for the addresses you serve.  This mail gateway should
minimally use the bl.spamcop.net and dnsbl.sorbs.net blacklists
to reduce spam influx.  I also recommend setting up sqlgrey on
your mail gateway which will give you greylisting.  Look up
razor and set up spamassassin.

I'm assuming that you want an email address for private 
personal use.  Do it yourself email gives you control
and privacy.

BTW, I suggest learning about domain keys even though it's
something I don't know anything about as it is apparently
quite useful in the fight against spam.

If I'm totally off on this one, why do you want a publicly
hosted email account via a third party?

     --  Michael C. Robinson



From creswick at gmail.com  Thu Aug 14 00:15:37 2008
From: creswick at gmail.com (Rogan Creswick)
Date: Thu, 14 Aug 2008 00:15:37 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Need new e-mail account
In-Reply-To: <1218696844.24259.8.camel@goose.robinson-west.com>
References: <20080813223941.112fa1eb.johnxj@comcast.net>

On Wed, Aug 13, 2008 at 11:54 PM, robinson-west user
<plug_1 at robinson-west.com> wrote:
> How about running your own mail server?

*Unless* you have an intense desire to understand how email systems
work, I suggest leaving that up to someone else.  It's pretty easy to
set up a server that will send/receive your test messages, but it is
significantly more difficult to keep it working properly, spam-free
(where "spam-free" is defined by gmail's spam filtering performance,
or some similar level of quality), safe, and functional.

It's very easy to learn just enough to do damage. (I've fallen into
the trap of thinking "oh, it'll be easy...." and 6 months later lost
all email access because I didn't have backup MX records set properly,
and my UPS battery died, then later the cable modem was down for a
week, and finally my fans seized and the processors caught on fire
while I was gone.. $4!7 happens, and when it happens to your mail
server, you can loose important things...)

If you really want to, and since you're not using this address for
critical email, you could certainly go this route.  I just want to
warn you: it's not trivial.

My suggestion is to use the gmail web interface.  I didn't like it
much in the beginning, but it has grown on me, and the search features
are much better than anything I've found in desktop email clients.

--Rogan

> So now I am shopping for a replacement free e-mail account. I started
> with Gmail, but I can't get it configured so that Sylpheed can download
> messages.

Did you enable POP support on gmail? It's not by default, as is IMAP. 
You also need SSL enabled for incoming and outgoing and use the correct 
ports.

> An additional fact: When I am at PSU I cannot send e-mail unless I send
> it through mailhost at pdx.edu using my pdx.edu account.

You need to setup your username and password for outgoing too. Look at 
the setup on the gmail help pages for Thunderbird. It probably has all 
the info you need for Sylpheed.

logically. There is a tab for Send and a tab for Receive, plus a tab

not the Receive tab. The Send tab does have a separate box for username
and password, but you have to specify the send address on the Basic
tab.

Dear John, 

One intermediate option is to use your own domain - and have it hosted
by a third party. Such options can be fairly inexpensive - I have 500MB
of space from Brainhosting for this mommabears.com domain. I use it
mostly for experiments and email for $18/yr, along with $7/yr for the
domain. 

While it doesn't require you to run your own mail server, it does
require you to understand DNS forwarding. It has its own URL for sending
and receiving email as well.

Then you can set up as many email accounts as you need - including
dedicated accounts for mailing lists, junk, etc. 

Thanks, 
Mike

John Jason Jordan wrote:

> I can't imagine ever needing more than the three accounts I have - my
> Comcast account, my business account, and the Gmail throwaway account. 
> 
> I realize there are people here who can't understand someone not
> needing dozens of e-mail accounts, but that's not me. Nor do I have
> time right now to learn all about how e-mail works.

I think the point Wes was trying to make was that for free (registration 
fees for the domain aside), you can have yourdomain.com with Google Apps 
for Domains hosting the site and your email for no cost. It's not about 
having dozens of accounts all over the place.

Here's the thing about email accounts. Many are not portable. Gmail (et 
al) is, but your Comcast isn't. If you move to DSL or to an area Comcast 
doesn't service, then you will lose the Comcast email account. By owning 
your own domain, your email addresses are not based on your ISP. You 
could move to another country and always keep your email addresses. For 
some, this isn't important. For others, keeping the same email address 
forever is.

Setting this up with Google is slightly more difficult than registering 
the domain. You get the benefits of not learning about mail servers, 
having google's excellent spam filtering and storage, email addresses 
that stay for as long as you want, for very little cost.

-- 
- m0gely

Consider yourself lucky, I've had to change ISP several times over the past
few years, and many of those times it was not by choice, the cable company
(or the rights to the region we were in) was being bought and sold like a
hot potato.  This was back at my folk's house.  First we had a few small DSL
providers, PhoenixDSL was one (long gone now, email was @phoenixdsl.com or
something), and maybe one or two others, then we got cable, which was
through a local company MediaOne cable (email @mediaone.net)... they got
bought out by AT&T, so our emails again changed (@attbi.com), then they sold
this local portion of the county to Time Warner, so again our emails changed
(@socal.rr.com).  Needless to say I got rather sick of it and sometime
around there is when I got Gmail (it was just coming out of "alpha" by
then).  Also when I moved out we got DSL in So Cal (DSL Extreme), then we
moved up here (Portland), and we have Verizon DSL now.

After this discussion, I decided to try and see how easy it was to setup my
own domain email through Gmail, and lo and behold it is done, and it was
rather painless.  So now I can go to mail.mydomain.net, and sign in to a
custom Gmail site.  I can also setup IMAP or POP and check my own domain
email with Thunderbird or any regular email client.  Very spiffy.

On Fri, Aug 15, 2008 at 7:35 AM, Richard C. Steffens <rsteff at comcast.net> wrote:
> But my grandpa had it worse. When he wanted to send a message to
> someone, he had to build a fire, throw on some wet wood, and then
> alternately cover and uncover the fire with a blanket!

We still do that here when the 'net goes down -- the only difference
is that instead of stocking the fire with wood, we just pull the fans
off of a couple of P3's ;)

To get slightly back on topic --

John et al. can often get the benefit of multiple email accounts
(improved filtering) with gmail by appending unique strings to your
gmail user name when you give out your email address.  eg; if your
email address is jjj at gmail.com, then you can send email to
jjj+<anything>@gmail.com and it will show up in your in box.

You can then easily filter on the TO: field to keep emails separate.
For example, when I register at a website I don't fully trust, I'll
use a variation of my email address (eg: creswick+foo at gmail.com) and
then set up gmail to label all email to that address.  If the address
gets sold to spammers, then it's trivial to auto-archive or
auto-delete everything that comes to that address.

--Rogan

throwing out the personal mail I send to my friends who happen 
to be Yahoo subscribers.  So if you have a Yahoo mail account,
I probably can't send email to you.  While you may consider that
a blessing :-), it also means that other people that run their
own small servers may not be able to send email to you as well.

Oh well.  Time to use my seldom touched emergency gmail account
to tell friends and relatives currently on Yahoo to also get
gmail accounts so I can continue to communicate with them.
Strangely, mail to Yahoo groups still works.

From alan at clueserver.org  Sat Aug 16 18:13:43 2008
From: alan at clueserver.org (Alan)
Date: Sat, 16 Aug 2008 18:13:43 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] ANOUNCEMENT: PLUG Advanced Topics August 20th, 2008 7pm
Message-ID: <1218935623.6185.25.camel@rotwang>

PLUG Advanced Topics Meeting
Date: August 20th, 2008
Time: 7pm - 9pm-ish

Location: Jax Bar
          826 SW 2nd Ave
          Portland, OR
          http://www.jaxbar.com/
         


Speaker: Jonathan Leto <jaleto at gmail.com>

Title: Creating CPAN Modules with SWIG
 
Abstract:
This talk will assume a basic familiarity with Perl and C syntax and
go through the process of creating a CPAN module which uses the
Simplified Wrapper Interface Generator (SWIG) to make an interface
to an existing C library. To be used as a "live" example is Math::GSL,
a Perl module which is part of the Google Summer of Code 2008 
and provides an interface to the GNU Scientific Library.

Happy hour food prices for the first hour.

Standard meeting rules apply.

From creswick at gmail.com  Mon Aug 18 14:04:56 2008
From: creswick at gmail.com (Rogan Creswick)
Date: Mon, 18 Aug 2008 14:04:56 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Odd emacs feature...
Message-ID: <c834ec80808181404y40c07f7p18c0101ee0397852@mail.gmail.com>

I ran into an odd emacs feature the other day, and I'm not really sure
how to figure out what it is, or ... well, anything about it.  It's
likely new in emacs v23, so YMMV if you try it.  Cutting to the chase,
you can highlight content in a buffer in a more or less persistent way
by doing a funny little dance with the mouse and meta:

   * Click and drag a selection with the mouse, but don't release the
mouse button.
   * Press and hold Meta
   * Release the mouse button
   * Release Meta.
   * Ooh and Ahh over the selection that is now in yellow (at least,
it's yellow for me.)

Once you've finished oogling, you can either spend the next 30 min.
trying to get rid of that annoying yellow patch you just created, or
you can just repeat the above process minus the dragging.  (Press the
mouse button, press meta, release mouse, release meta).

Does anyone grok this thing? Is it really just a way to draw attention
to a portion of text? What is it called? (The built-in help features
aren't doing me any good here, since it's not exactly a single,
unambiguous, key binding, and it's obviously not the same as the
selection or point & mark.)

(This is not it, but it's also cool:
http://www.cs.cmu.edu/cgi-bin/info2www?(emacs)Highlight Interactively
)

--Rogan

On Mon, 18 Aug 2008, frank hunt wrote:

> Not sure where to look.  Primary user's junk mail is captured and
> redirected to the garbage collector user.  Just noticed that a message
> got through to another user.  The subject contained  the requisite
> *****SPAM***** notification.  Ideas?

Your mail log is a good place to start. You should be able to see the 
expected sequence of events for the primary user then compare it what 
occurred for the other user.

You might also check to see if there are different user preferences 
specified in each user's $HOME/.spamassassin/user_prefs file.

[global]
         workgroup = HOME
         server string = %h server (Samba, Fedora Core 9)
         wins support = yes
         interfaces = lo, eth0, vmnet8, vmnet1
         bind interfaces only = yes
         log file = /var/log/samba/%m.log
         socket options = TCP_NODELAY SO_RCVBUF=8192 SO_SNDBUF=8192
         hostname lookups = yes
         dns proxy = no
         obey pam restrictions = yes

         load printers = yes
         printing = cups
         printcap name = cups

[printers]
         comment = All Printers
         path = /var/spool/samba
         browseable = no
         public = yes
         guest ok = yes
         writable = no
         printable = yes

[print$]
         comment = Printer Drivers
         path = /etc/samba/drivers
         browseable = yes
         guest ok = no
         read only = yes
         write list = root

for smb.conf.

I get access denied, unable to connect under W2K pro.  Where do the
print drivers go for automatic installation and where do I get them
from?  Supposedly, the print$ share is supposed to export the
drivers.  I'm running samba-3.2.0-2.17.fc9.i386 on my system.
I think swat needs a major overhaul and improved cups integration.

The printer works under cups on the Linux side.

      Michael C. Robinson

From heinlein at madboa.com  Wed Aug 20 12:48:16 2008
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Wed, 20 Aug 2008 12:48:16 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Cups won't allow local printing.
In-Reply-To: <20080820121846.0os0qu6co488ogwk@web.robinson-west.com>
References: <20080820121846.0os0qu6co488ogwk@web.robinson-west.com>
Message-ID: <alpine.OSX.1.10.0808201243520.33279@guild.galois.com>

On Wed, 20 Aug 2008, someone wrote:

> [dad at silene samba]$ lp smb.conf
> lp: Unauthorized
> [dad at silene samba]$
>
> I'm on a Fedora Core 9 system that is fully updated.  According to 
> cups documentation, this is supposed to work.  SELinux is turned off 
> and there are no iptables rules.

My troubleshooting steps would be

  1. Ensure cups is running: /sbin/service cups status

  2. Check the logs, probably in /var/log/cups.

  3. http://localhost:631/ -- make sure printers are defined, etc.

  4. strace -o /tmp/lp.trace lp /etc/samba/smb.conf, then examine
     the trace log you just wrote to /tmp for indications of where
     the failure occurred

-- 
Paul Heinlein <> heinlein at madboa.com <> http://www.madboa.com/

From raanders at acm.org  Wed Aug 20 14:02:18 2008
From: raanders at acm.org (Roderick A. Anderson)
Date: Wed, 20 Aug 2008 14:02:18 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] video TO and keyboard/mouse FROM a laptop
Message-ID: <48AC865A.1000400@acm.org>

I have several machines that run headless or connected to a KVM and the 
colo.  I'm adding more and will be running out of ports on the KVM.

Is there any kind of an adapter to let me use a laptop as the video, 
keyboard and mouse for another computer.  I've seen mention of network 
based KVM switches but would only need/want to connect to one system at 
a time.

That make any sense?  Turn a laptop into a monitor, keyboard, and mouse 
for another system.


TIA,
Rod
-- 


From creswick at gmail.com  Wed Aug 20 14:18:16 2008
From: creswick at gmail.com (Rogan Creswick)
Date: Wed, 20 Aug 2008 14:18:16 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] video TO and keyboard/mouse FROM a laptop
In-Reply-To: <48AC865A.1000400@acm.org>
References: <48AC865A.1000400@acm.org>
Message-ID: <c834ec80808201418t41e73c31sbed3f9cd314135bf@mail.gmail.com>

On Wed, Aug 20, 2008 at 2:02 PM, Roderick A. Anderson <raanders at acm.org> wrote:
> That make any sense?  Turn a laptop into a monitor, keyboard, and mouse
> for another system.

VNC (or NX) should do the trick--*if* you only need to work on working
systems ;).  Just run a vnc server on each machine you want to connect
to, and use a client on the laptop.  You can probably toss something
into /etc/hosts.deny on each machine to prevent anything other than
your laptop from connecting via vnc.

If you don't want to monkey with cables to get BIOS / etc. then you
could *probably* set up a serial console and interface with that from
the laptop as well, but that is bound to be at least a bit of work
(depending on the capabilities of the machines you need to work on).

Aside from serial, I don't know of any way to work on a broken machine
w/out a set of devices connected to it directly or via kvm.

--Rogan

From scratchcomputing at gmail.com  Wed Aug 20 15:30:42 2008
From: scratchcomputing at gmail.com (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Wed, 20 Aug 2008 15:30:42 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] video TO and keyboard/mouse FROM a laptop
In-Reply-To: <4145b6790808201419o536e104dx405adec632f01cc6@mail.gmail.com>
References: <48AC865A.1000400@acm.org>
	<4145b6790808201419o536e104dx405adec632f01cc6@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <200808201530.42912.ewilhelm@cpan.org>

# from Robert Citek
# on Wednesday 20 August 2008 14:19:

>On Wed, Aug 20, 2008 at 4:02 PM, Roderick A. Anderson 
<raanders at acm.org> wrote:
>> I have several machines that run headless or connected to a KVM and
>> the colo. ?I'm adding more and will be running out of ports on the
>> KVM.
>>
>> That make any sense? ?Turn a laptop into a monitor, keyboard, and
>> mouse for another system.
>
>Yes, what you are asking makes perfect sense.  And I've been looking
>for something like that for years without success.

Well, a monitor, keyboard, and mouse could be plugged and unplugged from 
any system you want.  With the addition of some tape and possibly 
hinges they could even be made to resemble a laptop.

But it doesn't make much sense in the context of running out of ports on 
the kvm.  If you just want to graphically interface to them, but don't 
have anything to plug them into, you have to run a vnc server on the 
headless machine, which makes any sort of low-level task far too 
interesting because losing network or whatever means your vnc 
connection goes poof.

So, to get to the low-level functionality via the network as if you were 
sitting at the machine, you need some pricey hardware which is itself 
essentially a networked computer:

  http://www.realweasel.com/

There might be some other gizmos which you can plug into the K,V, and M 
ports but by the time you get a few of those, one of those fancy +8-way 
networked KVM gizmos starts to sound like a good deal.

>Is there any kind of an adapter to let me use a laptop as the video, 
>keyboard and mouse for another computer.  I've seen mention of network 
>based KVM switches but would only need/want to connect to one system at 
>a time.

Oh, just once?  Seems like there should be enough wires on the parallel 
port to pull that off in software, but perhaps a bit of a chip and usb 
would cleaner (and you might need enough active circuitry that any sort 
of software touching the vga and PS/2 pins directly would just make a 
mess of it all anyway.)

But I would think using one of your existing kvm's cables as a rogue 
would be the way to go if you can actually be bothered to mess with all 
of the business of dragging wires around inside the cabinet while being 
careful not to snap off an ethernet connector on any of the production 
servers.

--Eric
-- 
The only thing that could save UNIX at this late date would be a new $30
shareware version that runs on an unexpanded Commodore 64.
--Don Lancaster (1991)

    http://scratchcomputing.com

From daehlie at gmail.com  Wed Aug 20 16:14:23 2008
From: daehlie at gmail.com (Kirk Harr)
Date: Wed, 20 Aug 2008 16:14:23 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] video TO and keyboard/mouse FROM a laptop
In-Reply-To: <200808201530.42912.ewilhelm@cpan.org>
References: <48AC865A.1000400@acm.org>
	<4145b6790808201419o536e104dx405adec632f01cc6@mail.gmail.com>
	<200808201530.42912.ewilhelm@cpan.org>
Message-ID: <6edf64990808201614n23ca836dw22fc5df71febe603@mail.gmail.com>

Both Raritan and Avocent sell IP KVMs that use CAT5 as the interconnect and
are basically a glorified switch with a couple video adapters and a web
interface built in. The machines use a cat5 -> vga/usb or vga/ps2 dongles
that connect to the servers and pull power over PoE. While this does sound
all WHIZ-BANG! and all, their browser plugins to control the servers over
the network are buggy, and the DSView Software you need to take advantage of
the Avocent gear is not a trivial investment. I ended up scrapping both
raritan and avocent and just provisioning a VLAN for all the IPMI
controllers our servers had and used those for console level access.

Kirk Harr

# from Scott Van Hoosen
# on Friday 22 August 2008 12:02:

>I have a co-worker that would like to know if there is a Linux
> equivalent to Solidworks. Any suggestions?

You want that open source, or just "runs on Linux"?  The term "3D CAD" 
is also very ambiguous.  For what purpose?  Parametric and relational 
modeling, solids or surfaces, mechanical or architectural?

There is brlcad if you're hoping to model the ballistic penetration 
resistance of tank armor, blender if you want to make video game 
models, Pro-E if you want to write a big check, Varcon, etc.

Sorry I wasn't clearer before. He uses Solidworks to create 3D models of mechanical objects of production parts, including dimensions of the model. It does not need animation, nor does it need to calculate forces or anything. It would need to export the model in some industry-standard format to be sent to a manufacturer to build the part.

It does not have to be free or open source, though that is a big plus. "Runs on Linux" is the key in this situation.

Modeling to specific dimensions and dimensioning (for printing working 
drawings used in traditional fabrication) are different things.

making STL files, but doesn't seem to have much in the way of 
parametric design.  VariCAD will probably be more suited to parts 
engineering.

be copied and distributed without restrictions"... ok, but can I change 
it?  kostenlos weitergegeben werden?

From heinlein at madboa.com  Mon Aug 25 07:54:15 2008
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Mon, 25 Aug 2008 07:54:15 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Preventing Probes Like This
In-Reply-To: <48B29FE3.4020803@gisnet.com>
References: <48B29FE3.4020803@gisnet.com>
Message-ID: <alpine.OSX.1.10.0808250748370.2704@orange.madboa.com>

On Mon, 25 Aug 2008, Bill Thoen wrote:

> Anyone have any ideas on how to prevent probe attempts like this one
> from succeeding?
>
> From 66.40.56.32:
>
> /index.php?url=../../../../../../../../../../../../../etc/passwd%00 HTTP Response 200

If index.php will never take any arguments, and assuming you're 
running Apache, this will work:

   RedirectMatch  gone  ^/index\.php\?.*$

The "gone" returns an HTTP 410 error, "indicated that the resource has 
been permanently removed." You can, however, return any numeric status 
code you want.

-- 
Paul Heinlein <> heinlein at madboa.com <> www.madboa.com


From tim-pdxlug at sentinelchicken.org  Mon Aug 25 08:11:32 2008
From: tim-pdxlug at sentinelchicken.org (Tim)
Date: Mon, 25 Aug 2008 08:11:32 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Preventing Probes Like This
In-Reply-To: <alpine.OSX.1.10.0808250748370.2704@orange.madboa.com>
References: <48B29FE3.4020803@gisnet.com>
	<alpine.OSX.1.10.0808250748370.2704@orange.madboa.com>
Message-ID: <20080825151132.GB2455@sentinelchicken.org>


> > Anyone have any ideas on how to prevent probe attempts like this one
> > from succeeding?
> >
> > From 66.40.56.32:
> >
> > /index.php?url=../../../../../../../../../../../../../etc/passwd%00 HTTP Response 200
> 
> If index.php will never take any arguments, and assuming you're 
> running Apache, this will work:
> 
>    RedirectMatch  gone  ^/index\.php\?.*$
> 
> The "gone" returns an HTTP 410 error, "indicated that the resource has 
> been permanently removed." You can, however, return any numeric status 
> code you want.


Why bother?  The key here is to have secure handling of the url
parameter.  Here are some approaches you should consider, in order, to
avoid path traversal issues:

1. Don't include any user-supplied values in filesystem paths.  If a
   dynamic path is needed on the backend, use an array as a lookup table
   and have the page accept only specific keys into that table.

2. If you *have* to include user-supplied values in filesystem paths
   (which is actually very rare, you should reconsider), then take the
   value, normalize it as a path using built-in path routines (don't
   remember what PHP has for this) and only then concatenate it with
   your path prefix.


If your concern here is about a third-party PHP app that you've
installed and aren't sure how it works under the hood... well you should
think about trying something else.  I make a living out of breaking into
websites and something about the PHP platform encourages insecure coding
practicies.  There are so many incredibly insecure open source PHP apps
out there that you'd have to spend a lot of time and effort vetting it.
Filtering URLs for specific types of evil on specific pages is a lost
cause.  Perhaps try a Python, Ruby or J2EE app.


good luck,
tim


From bthoen at gisnet.com  Mon Aug 25 10:02:33 2008
From: bthoen at gisnet.com (Bill Thoen)
Date: Mon, 25 Aug 2008 11:02:33 -0600
Subject: [PLUG] Preventing Probes Like This
In-Reply-To: <20080825151132.GB2455@sentinelchicken.org>
References: <48B29FE3.4020803@gisnet.com>	<alpine.OSX.1.10.0808250748370.2704@orange.madboa.com>
	<20080825151132.GB2455@sentinelchicken.org>
Message-ID: <48B2E5A9.6050304@gisnet.com>

I learned my lesson several years about changing web pages using a 
passed URL with a PHP script, and now I don't pass anything at all 
between my web pages.  But apparently just using php for web pages is 
sort of like giving a monkey the keys to the banana plantation.  This 
guy just added ?url=../../etc. and seems to have gotten a good look at 
my password file. I don't think he has the actual encrypted passwords 
because I think they're supposed to be somewhere else, but exposing a 
valid list of user names is a lot more than I wanted to give out.

Every time I've gotten hacked it seems to have been through some hole 
I'd unknowingly left open in some neat new technology that sounded like 
a good idea at the time. Now I'm learning JavaScript; I can't wait to 
see how many holes the black hats find in that. I was planning on using 
a mix of PHP for the server side and JavaScript for the client side, but 
I don't know; maybe I should just post the root password in the title 
page and save time.

I don't want  to make a boring little html read-only web page. I'd like 
to use my server to its fullest potential and not be intimidated by the 
predators out there.  But there's no grace period for newbies anymore. 
Make one tiny mistake, and you're lunch. What also annoys me is that 
when you want to learn how to do something, and buy the forty-dollar, 
5-lb book from SAMS or WROX or whoever, it's usually already out of 
date, and they seldom supply you with details about all the millions of 
ways that the great software they're promoting can be compromised. No 
wonder there's brigade-sized bot-nets out there. It's so easy for the 
hackers to press-gang new machines!

Hackers are like mosquitoes; we'll never get rid of them, they'll suck 
you dry if they can, and I guess if you want to play on the 'net, you've 
got to expect to have to defend yourself. I suppose if somebody wrote a 
book on the many ways that systems can be hacked, it would just breed 
more kiddies and not enough newbies would read it before they got hacked.

Oh well, I suppose it's just one more brick in the wall... I guess I'll 
amend that redirect trick and block any attempt at using index.php with 
a '?' after it.

Thanks for the tip!
- Bill Thoen

From tim-pdxlug at sentinelchicken.org  Mon Aug 25 10:21:32 2008
From: tim-pdxlug at sentinelchicken.org (Tim)
Date: Mon, 25 Aug 2008 10:21:32 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Preventing Probes Like This

Message-ID: <20080825172132.GC2455@sentinelchicken.org>

Hi Bill,

> But apparently just using php for web pages is 
> sort of like giving a monkey the keys to the banana plantation.

Yes, exactly.

> Hackers are like mosquitoes; we'll never get rid of them, they'll suck 
> you dry if they can, and I guess if you want to play on the 'net, you've 
> got to expect to have to defend yourself. I suppose if somebody wrote a 
> book on the many ways that systems can be hacked, it would just breed 
> more kiddies and not enough newbies would read it before they got hacked.

Those books are already out there and you are right, far too few
programmers read into these things.  Consider checking out owasp.org for
some free secure programming advice.

It is possible to write a secure PHP app that does complicated things.
Don't get me wrong.  I was a PHP developer for a number of years.
The problem with it, as I see it, is that nearly every interface and API
built into the language is insecure by default... the easiest way to use
it is the unsafe way.  You have to put extra effort in to make it
secure, which means newbies invariably mess it up.  The plethora of
"helpful" suggestions by random users on the PHP manual websites doesn't
help either, since fully 2/3rds of them are complete crap.

Other platforms have a more secure-by-default mentality where the
easiest way to use an API also happens to be the secure way. 

If you're not an aspiring security nerd and don't want to have to learn
about every type of vulnerability under the sun, I strongly suggest
trying out other open source web development platforms.  Java/J2EE stuff
is a good way to go if you want to build a solid app and don't mind
taking your time doing it.  You'd definitely want to use a data
validation framework, such as struts, with this.

I personally use mod_python for quite a bit of stuff, but it's not the
easiest to get started with either since you probably will want to write
your own handler and page templating. 

Ruby on rails is popular, though I'm not very familiar with it.

> Oh well, I suppose it's just one more brick in the wall... I guess I'll 
> amend that redirect trick and block any attempt at using index.php with 
> a '?' after it.

Once again, that's just a bandaid.  Use it until you make your app
secure, but don't make a habit of it.

HTH,
tim


From creswick at gmail.com  Mon Aug 25 10:25:33 2008
From: creswick at gmail.com (Rogan Creswick)
Date: Mon, 25 Aug 2008 10:25:33 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Preventing Probes Like This
In-Reply-To: <48B2E5A9.6050304@gisnet.com>
References: <48B29FE3.4020803@gisnet.com>
	<alpine.OSX.1.10.0808250748370.2704@orange.madboa.com>
	<20080825151132.GB2455@sentinelchicken.org>
	<48B2E5A9.6050304@gisnet.com>
Message-ID: <c834ec80808251025r44c95365xa309e3922bf1aab@mail.gmail.com>

On Mon, Aug 25, 2008 at 10:02 AM, Bill Thoen <bthoen at gisnet.com> wrote:
> Oh well, I suppose it's just one more brick in the wall... I guess I'll
> amend that redirect trick and block any attempt at using index.php with
> a '?' after it.

Er... that's not the right solution.  You're trying to fix a leaky
boat by drinking the water -- your feet may be dry now, but it's not
going to end well.

If you are writing the php app, then you should make it so that such
an attack *is not possible*.  The application itself should deny this
sort of thing -- by *never* trusting anything that you cannot
guarantee came from your server. (URLs, form fields, user names,
passwords, etc... these are all very, very dangerous places to get
inputs.)

Please, please, please, don't write another app that is only remotely
safe if you follow a laundry list of steps that set up a "secure"
environment.  You will invariably miss something (it happens to us
all) and the next person to install your app will also miss something,
or type a regular expression into their .htaccess file wrong, or need
to modify it so that requests to their wordpress blog still work...
etc.  (and that person may be you -- you are going to do a full
reinstall when your box gets rooted, right?)

If you are not the application author, then use a different
application and report the bug!

--Rogan

On Mon, 25 Aug 2008, Bill Thoen wrote:

> I don't want  to make a boring little html read-only web page. I'd like to

Bill,

   Allow me to suggest that you look at established frameworks for web sites
that are based on scripting languages other than PHP. We're using Ruby on
Rails for one service, and I know there are a bunch of Python-based
frameworks with a lot of support and experience.

   With many of these, web- and maillist-based resources are much more
current than are the dead tree printed versions. For non-moving targets, the
latter are ideal, but for stuff that changes every week a more nimble
resource is called for.

From daehlie at gmail.com  Mon Aug 25 11:14:04 2008
From: daehlie at gmail.com (Kirk Harr)
Date: Mon, 25 Aug 2008 11:14:04 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] CGI
In-Reply-To: <48B2DFBB.70904@verizon.net>
References: <48B2DFBB.70904@verizon.net>
Message-ID: <6edf64990808251114k34e3f064t77899d70d45a13ba@mail.gmail.com>

A Test CGI is usually a page that is used to determine if CGI handling for a
specific language is functioning. Like if you coded "<?php phptest(); ?> on
a page in a PHP environment it would generate a page with a byunch of debug
info and HTTP Headers that are visable to the server. I would doubt its
anything to worry about, its likely just left over from the server was being
setup.

Kirk Harr
